Special Telegraph Supplement

Shortwave

Shanghai-Guangdong Telephone Communication 196

— Lü Bing

In recent years, our country's construction industry has made rapid progress, especially in the development of transportation. Long-distance telephone occupies an important position in transportation. With the active management of the Ministry of Communications, and years of construction, it keeps pace with the times, and the telephone communication reaches all locations, no matter how far. The Nine-Province Telephone Network has been successfully connected, and the Shanghai-Hankou and Shanghai-Guangdong wireless telephones have also been officially opened for business one after another. Using wireless radio for long-distance conversations domestically is truly a first. However, Shanghai-Hankou still has wired telephone that can directly connect, while Shanghai-Guangdong does not. Therefore, the public's hope for telephone communication between Shanghai and Guangdong is more urgent than that for Shanghai-Hankou. Now that it has been achieved, the people of both places can use it for conversation, as if they were face to face, and their joy is beyond description!

It is also possible to erect copper wires and set up repeater stations between Shanghai and Guangdong for wired telephone communication, but the route is long, winding, and full of high mountains and ridges, making construction very difficult. Moreover, the demand for pole and wire materials is large, and the factory costs are huge, which is not permitted by the current economy. Therefore, the Ministry of Communications plans to first set up telephone stations in Shanghai, Hankou, and Guangdong, and install telephone equipment for mutual connection, so that in the midst of economic considerations, the convenience of free response can still be achieved. Wired and wireless are originally one, complementing each other, and the effect is more obvious. When we first tried the Shanghai-Guangdong wireless telephone, listening to the clarity of the voice and feeling the perfection of the reception, it was really no different from wired telephone communication.

Southern Guangdong is rich in resources, and its politics and commerce occupy an important position in the country. In the past, due to the obstruction of mountains and the poor transportation, it was easy for Middle Wu (Jiangsu and Zhejiang area) and the local areas to be estranged. As a result, warlords took the opportunity to seize power and monopolize Southern Guangdong, and the national territory seemed to be in a separate state, another world. With the communication of this wireless radio, the so-called Southern Guangdong is just in the same room. Conversation is convenient, and accumulated feelings can be expressed. What more estrangement of opinions can there be?

Around Christmas 197

— Han Shui

Time flies like an arrow, and this year's Christmas is coming again in the blink of an eye. Although Christmas is a Western festival, once Christmas has passed, the New Year is approaching. Christmas and the New Year are only a few days apart, so celebrating Christmas and New Year's greetings are often linked and inseparable.

Those who are good at socializing will certainly not let Christmas and New Year pass easily. Before Christmas, they often prepare how to extend greetings between the two places to express mutual feelings. Thus, they either send gifts, or greeting cards, or, for more grand occasions, send Christmas and New Year's telegrams.

Using telegrams to congratulate the New Year is a common social practice in Western countries. They believe that sending just a printed card to close relatives and friends who live far apart, signing one's own name, seems too simple and not enough to express warm sincerity. Therefore, they abandon the use of cards and use telegrams instead. These New Year's telegrams are handwritten and signed very solemnly. If they are sent to and arrive in a remote place, they can use facsimile telegrams, and they must be delivered by facsimile so that the person receiving the New Year's greetings can see their handwriting in person, as if they were seeing the person in person, which of course can bring great joy.

Those who travel between Christmas and the New Year especially hope that close relatives and friends will send New Year's telegrams so that they can find some comfort in the lonely journey. Therefore, ships sailing in the ocean often receive many telegrams from wireless machines around December 25, congratulating passengers. Passengers on long journeys often read and reread telegrams from relatives, friends, or loved ones, reluctant to let go, leaving a very deep impression in their minds.

In addition, those who have contacts with people abroad, or those who have business relationships, on the occasion of this grand Christmas and New Year, mutual congratulations cannot be expressed without telegrams. If it is just a card, delivered far away by mail, it is not only delayed, but the recipient will also regard it as ordinary and not value it. In short, Christmas and New Year's telegrams have their wonderful use, and can never be equated with a piece of card.

A Respectful Announcement to City Telephone Subscribers and Long-Distance Telephone Callers 198

— Shan Ronghai

When managing a certain business, certain disputes are bound to occur. This is not a bad phenomenon of poor business management, but a trend that is unavoidable in the business process. The same is true for managing the telephone business. However, once such disputes are explained, both parties can understand. Now, let me try to explain it as follows:

(A) Regarding City Telephones, there are the following two types:

(1) Disputes regarding the operator's reply of "wait a moment" (referring to non-automatic telephones) – Every time a subscriber encounters a situation where they call a certain number, and the operator replies "wait a moment", they often mistakenly believe that the operator is deliberately making things difficult, and express a bad impression. How can it be known that in the aspect of the operator, the connection between the two telephones is just a matter of inserting the plug, so why make things difficult? When they call a certain number, if there is already a plug in the port of that number, it means that the number is already talking to another subscriber, so how can it be connected again? Once this type of dispute is explained, it will be clear. It is the same with automatic telephones, that when a certain number is talking to another number, it cannot be connected to other numbers.

(2) Disputes regarding subscribers not reporting the number but only calling the name of the household (referring to non-automatic telephones) – Some subscribers do not want to search for the number of the called subscriber in the phone book, and only call the name of the household for connection. In the operator's aspect, they must ask the subscriber to report the number in order to comply with the regulations. Because the operator's mind cannot memorize so many subscriber numbers. As a result, the subscriber thinks that the operator is not courteous, and complaint letters flood in. However, it is not known that the printing and distribution of the phone book by the bureau is for each subscriber to look up the numbers. Now, they abandon the phone book and only report the household name. I ask, can the operator's memory be so extensive? It is the same with automatic telephones, if they do not know the number of the called party, can they dial it and connect? Therefore, it is an inappropriate habit for the calling subscriber to only report the household name. It should be removed in order to avoid this unnecessary dispute.

(B) Regarding Long-Distance Telephones, there are also the following two types:

(1) Calculation of Call Time – Long-distance callers often have disputes over the calculation of call time: for example, if the bureau thinks that five minutes should be counted as two charges, they will insist that it has not reached three minutes and should be counted as one charge. This kind of dispute is indeed a normal human emotion, but they do not know that the bureau calculates the time completely impartially. Moreover, state-run enterprises are far from comparable to other commercial enterprises that only aim at trade profits. All kinds of regulations are announced by law, how can the bureau arbitrarily change them? Moreover, for a long-distance telephone call, both the caller and the receiver must register the time. How can the bureau's staff arbitrarily increase or decrease the time and commit a crime against the regulations? However, this kind of dispute also has its considerable main reason, because when the caller is paying attention to the conversation, they do not realize that the time has passed so quickly. They think that they have only talked a few sentences, so how can it have already been four or five minutes? But the bureau staff should be trusted, and they will never arbitrarily increase or decrease the time. Therefore, some callers sometimes insist on asking the bureau for evidence of the duration of the call, which is an unavoidable factor in disputes. Regarding this point, the ministry is now trying to adopt a time-stamping machine, which will surely satisfy the callers.

(2) Disputes over Waiting for Connection – On busy lines, callers become anxious and angry due to the long wait for connection, and there are many complaints, even those who roar in the waiting area! Regarding this point, it is indeed a phenomenon that occurs because the country's construction has not yet fully developed, which causes inconvenience to the public. However, the ups and downs of business are like the tides, sometimes one line is enough to cope with the demand, and sometimes even ten lines are not enough. Therefore, the waiting for connection of callers is a phenomenon that exists in all countries. Fortunately, the current regulations stipulate that if it exceeds two hours, the number can be cancelled free of charge. If it can be connected within these two hours, it is already a good phenomenon of today's material civilization. We really don't need to be anxious and angry, and still complain that we have been waiting for too long. If there is really no time to wait, you may as well send a telegram instead, which is also a remedy. I sincerely hope that callers and receivers will have a deep understanding of this point.

The Issue of Cancelling Long-Distance Telephone Numbers 199

— Jiong

Telephone bureaus or telegraph bureaus that also handle long-distance telephones (hereinafter referred to as the "telephone bureau") may cancel a caller's registered number, due to their request or because the long-distance call could not be connected, and may charge or exempt the caller from a cancellation fee, depending on the circumstances. Detailed regulations are already in place in the current "Domestic Long-Distance Telephone Business Regulations" of the Ministry of Communications, which are explained as follows:

(1) Situations in which a cancellation fee should be charged according to regulations:

(A) The called party should be rung up – If the long-distance telephone number of a certain place is dialed, after the calling bureau connects to the receiving bureau, the receiving bureau rings up the city telephone of the called party, but the called subscriber does not answer or deliberately does not answer, the fault is not with the telephone bureau. Therefore, if the call cannot be connected due to the above situation, the number should be cancelled immediately, and the caller should pay the cancellation fee according to the regulations.

(B) The designated telephone number is vacant – If the long-distance telephone subscriber designates the other party's telephone number, and the receiving bureau confirms that the number is indeed vacant and cannot be connected, the telephone bureau is not responsible. Therefore, the caller must pay the cancellation fee according to the regulations for this registered number that could not be connected.

(C) Calls that the telephone bureau cannot relay – If the caller designates the address of the called party, and the receiving bureau sends someone to relay the call to the address, but the called party cannot be relayed because the address is wrong or incomplete, the telephone bureau has fulfilled its responsibility to relay the call. Therefore, if the caller receives a notification from the telephone bureau that the called party cannot be relayed, and the call cannot be connected, they must pay the cancellation fee according to the regulations.

(D) The called party is not called, or does not wish to answer – If the caller designates the called party, and the receiving bureau sends someone to the called party's address as stated by the calling bureau. If both the called party and their designated representative are away on business, and no one comes to answer the call, or if the called party does not wish to answer the call from the calling party, the caller must pay the cancellation fee according to the regulations if they are notified by the telephone bureau that the called party could not be called or does not wish to answer the call, resulting in the call not being able to be connected.

(E) The caller does not answer – After the caller registers with the telephone bureau to call a long-distance number from a city telephone or private line, the receiving bureau has already called the called party, and the calling bureau has also rung the calling party's city or private line telephone, but the calling party is away on urgent business, so they are unable to answer the telephone bureau's return call; or if the caller has been notified by the telephone bureau that the called party has been called, but suddenly does not wish to answer the call for some reason, resulting in the call not being able to be connected, they should immediately pay the cancellation fee according to the regulations.

(F) The called party delays answering – If the called party of a long-distance telephone call does not go to answer the call within one hour of receiving notification from the telephone bureau, the telephone bureau will cancel the number immediately and collect a cancellation fee from the caller according to the regulations.

(G) The address of the called party is too far from the telephone bureau – According to Article 5 of the current "Domestic Long-Distance Telephone Business Regulations" of the Ministry of Communications, relayed calls are limited to those where the called party is within the business area of the telephone bureau, and for those without a fixed business area, the limit is 3 kilometers from the bureau. If the receiving bureau confirms that the address of the called party designated by the caller for a relayed call exceeds the above-mentioned distance, the receiving bureau will not be able to send someone to relay the call, and therefore the caller must also pay the cancellation fee according to the regulations if the call cannot be connected.

Although the above-mentioned circumstances in which the called party and the caller cannot connect are extremely complex, the reasons are nothing more than that one of the called or calling parties is unable to come to answer the call, or does not wish to answer the call. Since the telephone bureau has fulfilled its responsibility to call and relay the call, it is not responsible, so the current "Domestic Long-Distance Telephone Business Regulations" of the Ministry of Communications stipulates that if any of the above-mentioned circumstances occur, the telephone bureau may cancel the number and collect a cancellation fee from the caller.

(2) Situations in which cancellation fees are waived according to regulations:

(A) Telephone line damage – After the caller informs the telephone bureau of the called location name, telephone number or the name and address of the called party, the type of call, and the caller’s telephone number and address, if the calling bureau experiences an obstruction of the long-distance telephone or the phone equipment, which causes them not to connect to the receiving bureau and receiving party, the caller may request the cancellation of the number, and the cancellation fee will be waived. (To be continued)

New Long-Distance Telephone Regulations Effective This Month 200

Cancellation Methods Are Stipulated. There are Eleven Improvement Points.

The Ministry of Communications' newly revised "Domestic Long-Distance Telephone Business Regulations" will officially come into effect on the first of this month. This new regulation has many improvements. The differences between this regulation and the old regulation are recorded as follows:

(1) When a long-distance telephone's receiver is called and is in the midst of a city telephone call, the receiving bureau can seek the receiver's approval and interrupt their city telephone call, and connect the long-distance phone call.

(2) The old regulation's long-distance call that dials to a certain place and certain number without specifying the individual receiving the call has been renamed to "Dialing Number Call". The old regulation's long-distance phone call that dials to a certain place and certain number, specifying that a certain individual is receiving, was named the "Pre-informed Telephone" and has been renamed the "Dialing Individual Call". Callers can understand and recognize phone call types now with this determination of "Dialing Number" and "Dialing Individual". Additionally, the old regulation's "Pre-arranged Phone Call" is renamed "Scheduled Telephone" and is being actively enacted.

(3) The old regulation stated that for "Pre-informed Telephone" calls, ordinary rates must be added by 1/3, and to relay or forward for "Forwarding Phone Call", a specially appointed fee of 1 jiao was required. The new regulations state that the cost for forwarding the telephone is the same as the dialing individual telephone, and there is no appointed individual cost.

(4) The new regulations' Cancellation Fees are cheaper than in the old regulations, and less than 1/3 of the ordinary dialing rate.

(5) The regulations for Ordinary Telephone Costs are for dialing. The costs for Relay phone calls, Dialing Individual phone calls, and Cancellation costs must be checked in the categorized cost comparison charts to avoid mistakes.

(7) Forwarding distances are limited to 3 kilometers away, decreasing from 2 kilometers prior, and the appointed forwarding costs are cancelled.

(8) Callers may change the type of phone call before receiving the notification for calls received. This is limited to changing ordinary phone calls to urgent ones, and changing dialing numbers to dialing an individual.

(9) Callers dialing individual calls can specify an alternate for the individual that is being dialed.

(10) Due to line congestion after a dialing registration, a waiting period of 2 hours for an ordinary call is required (previously, it was four hours), and a waiting period of 1 hour is required for an urgent call (previously, two hours) to receive a free cancellation.

(11) In busy circumstances, the limitation for continuous calls is limited to a maximum of 3 times.

The improvements above are to procedures or the cost adjustments, and all improvements for long-distance phone services.

Communication Ministry: Long-Distance Phone Locations Open on December 10: 201

In addition, Wu Yi and two locations, through Hangzhou and Wu Xing, have two locations that are transferring the area, with the Zhe area's Fuyang, Tonglu, Jiande, Chun'an Lanxi, Longyou, Yuhang, Lin'an, Yuqian, Tangxi, Changxing, Anji, and Wukang, and communications to these locations opened on December 10.

Ideal - Reality 202

— Small Offering

Reality—A telegram sent from Shanghai is delivered by the sender to the telegraph office, undergoes registration, transmission, reception, delivery, and other procedures, and ultimately reaches the recipient in Nanjing. The time taken is less than fifteen minutes.

Ideal—A telegram sent from Shanghai to Hankou, considering the distance, it would be expected to take at least an hour. A reply telegram would likely take several hours.

Reality—The telegram reaches the recipient in Hankou in just over ten minutes. A reply telegram is delivered within an hour.

Result—Reality exceeds expectations. The distance between the two places is not a reliable measure of the speed of telegram transmission. Common assumptions sometimes prove incorrect. The reason? Both Shanghai-Hankou and Nanjing-Shanghai have direct lines, allowing for direct operation, and communication is equally convenient.

"William Tell" 204

— Sen Yao

Although German literature has a very long history, its true maturity came after the seventeenth century, and its worldwide reputation, shining for generations, was truly achieved by the classical literary arts of the eighteenth century. Strictly speaking, their literature has only occupied a major place in the history of world literature for about one or two hundred years. Among the figures who contributed the most during this period were the so-called Six Great Poetic Heroes. Among them, besides Lessing, Wieland, and Goethe, Schiller was one of the founding members.

In Europe, German poetry always maintains the greatest honor. As for drama, especially tragedy and poetic drama, few other countries can compete. If one has an intention to delve into German literature, one must grasp these two subjects. Even if you only want to glimpse the outline of their literature, the drama of the eighteenth century is a must-know department. When it comes to the drama of this period, in addition to Goethe's Faust, Schiller's complete works occupy a completely important position.

Schiller (Friedrich Schiller, 1759-1805) was a natural poet, rich in reason, and good at contemplation. His plays have a rigorous structure and detailed content. He is generally regarded as Germany's greatest playwright. Although his poetic talent is slightly inferior to Goethe, his plays always surpass those of the poetic heroes—this is a consensus among critics.

Schiller's famous plays total nine, which can be arranged in the following order according to the date of publication: (1) The Robbers (Die Räuber); (2) Fiesco's Conspiracy (Die Verschwörung des Fiesco); (3) Intrigue and Love (Kabale und Liebe); (4) Don Carlos; (5) Wallenstein; (6) Maria Stuart; (7) The Maid of Orleans (Die Jungfrau von Orleans); (8) The Bride of Messina (Die Braut von Messina); (9) William Tell (Wilhelm Tell).

From this, we can know that among Schiller's plays, William Tell is the last one. Because the author's skills became more proficient and his thoughts matured, this play, once produced, was almost beyond criticism. Not only can it not be matched in the German classical school, but it is also difficult to find a selection in modern world drama. Because it has the most suitable qualities for performance, it is still a popular script on the stage.

Generally speaking, Schiller's works often have slightly profound words and sentences, and several plays are overly tinged with melancholy. Therefore, J. Macy has the following remarks in his A Story of World Literature:

"...criticism of its rhetoric and frequently found sentimentality is common... but the most beautiful plays, such as William Tell... are still vibrant, the lively things at the bottom of the play..."—according to Hu Zhongchi's translation.

Indeed, no matter how you nitpick Schiller's works, the greatness of William Tell cannot be denied by anyone.

William Tell is a historical tragedy, taken from a story in Swiss independence. When the Habsburg imperial family of Germany ruled over the areas of Schwyz, Uri, and Unterwalden, their appointed governor, Gessler, was a brutal and merciless man. He led a group of officials to implement various oppressive policies in Switzerland, causing the people to completely lose the freedom they considered inherent. Thus, a torch of revolution was waved among farmers, workers, and slaves. With the determination to unite against foreign aggression, they victoriously restored their freedom, expelled the tyrannical officials, and completed the foundation of independence.

In this play, William Tell appears as a strong, heroic, loving, and peaceful person. Relying on his skilled arrows and strong physique, he rescues his oppressed compatriots everywhere, and finally establishes the greatest achievement in fighting for freedom—assassinating Gessler. He originally had no old grudges against the rulers, and even respected the officials very much. It is said that once when he was hunting and passing through a wilderness, with no one around, Gessler suddenly came face to face alone. At this time, Gessler showed a look of surprise towards this enemy who had been severely punished for a minor offense, but the official therefore harbored a determination to kill him. When the people rose up in unison, he finally chose this most difficult and important task for justice and freedom. Undoubtedly, in this play, Schiller truly symbolizes the Swiss national spirit with this personality—neither resistant nor humble, upholding the middle path and following righteousness.

In China during this extraordinary period, I believe that there are still very few things that are suitable for every patriotic people to recite and can be as beautiful and cordial as this. Furthermore, only the Chinese of our time most need and can understand all the meanings in this play. It depicts the psychology of traitors, the ferocious faces of invaders, and their means of oppression. At the same time, it not only instructs us with a correct understanding, encourages our courage, and excites our souls, but finally, I hope that all people who "do not want to be slaves" can appreciate this great creation.

Reading Diary One 205

— Ruo Yin

Stories of National Crisis · Shi Ying · Kaiming Bookstore Publishing · Price 35 cents

A few days ago, my younger brother wrote to me from school, asking me to choose a few supplementary reading materials on history and geography for him. Yesterday afternoon, I took advantage of my free time to buy a copy of "Stories of National Crisis," recently published by Kaiming Bookstore, intending to send it to my younger brother. Last night, when I was about to go to bed, I leaned on the pillow and casually flipped through this book. Unexpectedly, as soon as I opened it, the author's sincere and passionate feelings for his own country and clear and simple writing style captured my attention, making me unconsciously read this small book in one breath within three hours. After reading it, I felt extremely moved. What I cannot forget the most are the following passages:

"...The incompetent officials in charge of foreign affairs in China were single-mindedly afraid and naturally complied with every request. As a result, China suffered great losses just in the treaties on paper. However, at that time, the Chinese people, because they had only just come into contact with foreign countries, had not yet forgotten their position and were still unwilling to obediently be slaves to other countries. Unlike those traitors who do not know what shame is, they are extremely respectful to foreigners, being more careful than a pug serving its master..."—Lecture 3, "Foreign Troops First Invade the Capital."

"Although China's officialdom and weapons were useless, it was not as easy as they thought for foreign troops to attack the capital. Unfortunately, when the Allied Forces attacked Tianjin and Beijing, only a few Chinese troops in the north resisted the enemy. Most of the troops were fighting the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom in the south, busy killing their own hungry brothers, and did not have time to rescue the north from the foreign troops' attack. Therefore, the Anglo-French Allied Forces easily advanced north..."—Ibid.

What the author describes is the situation seventy or eighty years ago, but is this situation in our country limited to seventy or eighty years ago?

"Japan is in the sea east of China, surrounded by clear sea waves. The fan-shaped Mount Fuji and the brilliant cherry blossoms show her natural scenery everywhere. Therefore, in ancient China, Japan was regarded as Penglai Island, where immortal beings lived, and there were also infatuated emperors who sent envoys there to visit the immortals. The immortals' elixir of immortality was not found, but most of Japan's culture was transmitted from China... Recently, European and American powers came to the East and forced the Eastern countries to open their doors to do business. Japan, like China, did not welcome them, but because their military force was not as good as theirs, their doors were finally opened... and were forced to conclude many unequal treaties with them. However, after Emperor Meiji ascended the throne in 1867, he worked hard to imitate the methods of the European and American powers, reformed and modernized, and industry and commerce developed day by day, and the national power also became stronger day by day..."—Lecture 6, "Ryukyu Becomes a Sacrifice."

In the past, Japan, like our country, was also invaded by "European and American powers," but it was able to reform and strengthen itself, not only no longer being bullied by others, but instead bullying our country, which really makes us a little ashamed!

"The British boast: 'Where the sun shines, the British flag flies.' We Chinese can also say the same: 'Where the sun shines, there are footprints of the Chinese.' But we Chinese cannot boast much. When people from other countries go abroad... carrying the mission of colonizing..., they have the government of their country as a bodyguard... Most of the overseas Chinese are hungry brothers in the country, unable to survive in the country, and have no choice but to cross the ocean to find a bite of bitter food. China naturally often suffers their abuse and expulsion. An overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia once said with tears: 'Our status in foreign countries is worse than that of a dog. A dog can still gnaw on the meat bones thrown by its master!'... In fact, we should say: 'Where the sun shines, there are blood, tears and bones of overseas Chinese.'"—Lecture 17, "Are We Only Good for Rolling Away?"

Our country is disappointing, causing our compatriots overseas to live a "subhuman" life, which naturally makes us heartbroken. In fact, given the current situation, if we do not work hard to save the country and survive, the entire nation will be reduced to a state of slavery.

"Anyone who sees the current situation in China will shake their heads and sigh, but I hope my readers will not do so. Some people think that the national crises of the past hundred years are all because China is not competitive enough and should not have allowed the powers to blast open the door during the Opium War; even if the door was blasted open, they should have awakened as soon as possible and embarked on the path of self-strengthening like Japan... It is true that some parts of China are not competitive enough, and it is also a fact that some Chinese are too mixed up. However, the common people of China are no worse than those of other countries, and we do not need to belittle ourselves too much; no nation in the world is born only fit to be slaves. Look at the contributions of the Chinese in the islands of Southeast Asia. The Chinese are truly the most hardworking, gentlest, and greatest nation... But if they do not rise up again, and the hungry brothers in the country continue to beat each other bloody, without thinking that the reason for not having food is the powers, then China truly has no hope."—Lecture 20, "Partition? Devour? Or Rejuvenation?"

"China is awake! The Chinese who are about to starve to death or become slaves are awake! The various national crises of the past are alarm bells to awaken us. We want to rejuvenate... We want to struggle out of the fate of starvation and slavery. There is only one way, that is to unite the four hundred million people and use our own flesh and blood to defeat the powers. Our hungry brothers, quickly stop killing each other. It is the powers that have been approaching us step by step for the past hundred years that have made us hungry. If we defeat the powers, everyone will have food to eat."—Ibid.

The author's conclusion is naturally correct, but in terms of the current situation, we must pay special attention to our most ferocious enemies among the powers and fully utilize the contradictions between other powers to attack the most ferocious enemies.

China in the Eyes of Foreigners 206

— Si Xi

It is said that foreigners often regard China as a "mysterious" country, and this is not without reason. China is large in area, has a large population, and has a complex and intricate social organization. It is not easy for foreigners to thoroughly understand, and even we Chinese ourselves do not understand it very clearly, especially in terms of the people's thinking. Fascists often regard them as easily tamed slaves, conspirators often regard them as easily ignited flames, pessimists often say they are dead ashes pulled out of the furnace, and optimists say they will be the red sun after a rainstorm. Everyone has their own opinions, everyone has their own reasons, but these reasons often do not have any reliable basis. Because their arguments are only based on their own purposes and do not start from actual experience.

But strangely enough, many of China's "mysteries" often need to be revealed by foreigners who think they don't understand them very well, such as the discovery of mineral resources in desolate mountains, the excavation of treasures in ancient tombs, etc.

Not only that, but also from "A Japanese View of China" (written by Japanese Uchiyama Kanzo, translated by Yu Bingqi, published by Kaiming Bookstore, price 35 cents), which I recently read, I saw a foreigner—the author—revealing many more important mysteries of our country—"the mystery of the people's feelings."

To be honest, Japanese research on China has indeed reached a very deep level. Just taking their diagnosis that our country's "big figures" all suffer from "Japanophobia" is enough for us to admire. But it seems to be the first time that "the people's feelings" have been portrayed so deeply as in this book.

The greatest characteristic of this book is that the author, unlike other Japanese, does not study China with selfish malice, but with the purpose of "taking the good and discarding the bad." But only in this way can his observations have unexpectedly profound places. He can see authentic "civilization" from what people think is "barbarism," and see complete "barbarism" from what people think is "civilization." His eyes directly penetrate into the hearts of the Chinese people, and his diagnosis is by no means like other similar books, only speculating from the surface. This is his unique point and the reason why he has created a new example in other Japanese books studying China.

The entire book contains thirty-two essays. Trying to analyze these texts one by one, we cannot help but admire the author's unique observations. The following points can be clearly pointed out:

First, he pointed out the expression of the Chinese people's idea of sympathy for the stage of division.

Since the end of the Qing Dynasty, the people of our country have been subjected to repeated natural disasters, man-made disasters, foreign insults, internal troubles, and the disturbance of traitors and local bullies, so that the property that ancestors had worked so hard to pass down for thousands of years was about to reach the point of "eating and selling everything." Except for a few capitalists, almost everyone is poor. In Europe and America, the property of an average family can be at least tens of thousands, but in China, how many people can be found among a hundred who have property worth more than ten thousand? Most people are so poor that they "don't know what will happen tomorrow." It is no longer surprising that an entire family commits suicide by poisoning because one person loses their job. Therefore, everyone has unconsciously developed the concept of "harmony and mutual assistance" to maintain each other. Therefore, they regard the misfortune of the poor as their own misfortune in the future, and use helping others as a preparation for others to help themselves in the future. This phenomenon is truly a good result earned by the people of the country through all kinds of hardships. But no one has mentioned it much, and this book is the first to do so.

The article "Buying Retail is Cheaper" says that the clerks in the store unconsciously have a kind of psychology that "people who can't afford to buy more must be poor," and they should "give more" goods, which creates the principle that buying retail is cheaper. "Pricing Based on the Person" says that small clerks do business and set prices based on the wealth of the buyer. "Leftovers" and "Another Leftover" say that it is reasonable for beggars to grab the leftovers from the meal service. "Life and Rights" uses the atrocities of the Shanghai Concession's abolition of shantytowns to refute the kindness of the military and civilians in the Chinese area outside the concession towards the poor. Each article relies on the author's own observations to explain and comment, and they are all very rare records.

Second, he pointed out a misunderstanding that is most likely to occur when foreigners first arrive in Shanghai.

Although there is only one article "Same Habits," its value is really great. It says that Japanese people who first arrive in Shanghai, because they don't speak the language and have heard that the rickshaw pullers in Shanghai are all bad guys, are careful to guard against them as soon as they get on the rickshaw. Occasionally, when the rickshaw passes through a dark alley or walks to a deserted place, they immediately think that the rickshaw puller is going to rob them. A preemptive mentality prompts them to start fighting, and as a result, a fierce fight occurs. The poor rickshaw puller not only doesn't get half a drop of blood money, but also suffers injuries, and even loses his life. Doesn't the Shanghai newspaper report a news story half a month ago about a British man beating a rickshaw puller to death? According to the British man's own confession, the reason is still here. The author now dissects the psychology of these passengers in detail and pleads for a great injustice for the innocent rickshaw pullers, which is really worthy of our admiration.

Third, he appropriately assesses Chinese customs and human feelings.

This may be the author's greatest purpose in writing this book. In "A Kind of Gang," he talks about the close concept of the Chinese people for "gangs," such as "Ningbo Gang" and "Guangdong Gang." "Three Kinds of Nature" says that the Chinese people are unwilling to be serious in doing things. "Convenient Tea" says that the Chinese people are intellectually pure. "Mutual Aid Banquet" says that the Chinese people have wonderful ways to deal with the costs of weddings, funerals, and birthdays. "The Words That a Limited Company Cannot Make a Profit" are very accurate:

"...As soon as a company is established, all the directors will pull their personal family relatives and related people into the company to eat the company's food... Even if Japanese companies have relatives and friends in positions, they have their own need to hold the position. After joining the company, each has its own duties... It is not the same in China... They just smoke cigarettes and take dry wages every day."

The author calls this situation "eating downism," which can be said to be extremely humorous. "Thorough Practical Life" implies that the Chinese love to calculate everything. ""A Certain Day's Transaction Talk" talks about the airs of the Chinese officialdom. "Is the Chinese Individualistic?" says that the Chinese have patience. "The Concept of Gambling" says that the mentality of Chinese and Japanese gamblers is different. "Words about Foreign Yarn," "Words about Ceiling," and "Failure If You Don't Devote All Your Strength" are all the author's insights from studying the psychology of Chinese merchants and customers. "Stealing and Falling" says "greasing palms." Others, such as "Fortune, Prosperity and Longevity," "Kidnapping," "Heaven Never Cuts Off All Hope," "Saying Thank You Loses Its Intimacy," "Labor-Management Coordination," "Needle Point and Fist," etc., all have interesting observations and appropriate diagnoses of our Chinese customs and human feelings. Due to space limitations, I can only ask readers to taste them for themselves.

As Mr. Lu Xun said in the preface, this book also has a shortcoming: "There is a tendency to say more about the advantages of China," but in some places, we can look at it from the opposite side and discover our own shortcomings.

As for his observations, of course, they cannot be very insightful everywhere. In some places, he has not yet touched the most profound realm. Such as in "Mutual Aid Banquet," he said:

"It is too far from the truth to say that Chinese people go bankrupt for half their lives because of weddings, and go bankrupt for the rest of their lives because of funerals..."

His reason is that the income from the gifts at each banquet can offset the expenses and have a surplus. Except for a few property owners, "most" are like this. In fact, it's not right. The more property owners there are, the more income they receive from gifts. The poorer people are, the more they have to lose their capital. Everyone knows this, because wealthy people naturally have more relatives and friends than people with no property, not to mention those who flatter and praise them. Before the "New Life" movement, didn't some "important people" deliberately create some celebrations to make money?

But in any case, this book is always a pioneering work that is worth reading for the Chinese people. It is the first book to delve into our Chinese people. We study Japan, only knowing to study its history and writing, but neglecting its people, just like they studied our country before this book. Now that we have read this book, we should also work harder ourselves!

Common Sense Everyone Should Possess 207

— Proverbs Four

Recently, a friend wrote to tell me that two lives were lost in his hometown. In one case, a daughter-in-law was slapped twice by her mother-in-law at the doorway. In response, the daughter-in-law secretly ate two boxes of red-head matches. When the poison took effect, it was the middle of the night. They wanted to send her to the hospital, but the hospital was in the city, more than ten miles away, and it was a dark night. Everyone was helpless, and as a result, a life was lost. In another case, a person fell into the river after getting drunk. People immediately rescued him, but he had swallowed a lot of water, and his breathing had stopped. The villagers didn't know anything about artificial respiration. As a result, they left him to his fate, and another life was lost.

My friend felt that everyone should have some common sense of first aid because of these two deaths. Therefore, he wrote to me, asking me to buy him two books so that he could read and study them himself, so that he could find ways to apply them when he encountered similar things in the countryside again. He said that saving a life is better than building a seven-story pagoda. In any case, he had to buy him a few books. I don't understand medical knowledge. It was really "asking a blind man for directions" for him to ask me to buy such first aid books. Fortunately, a colleague came to my residence, and I showed him the letter. He recommended two books published by Kaiming Bookstore: "Popular Medical First Aid" by Shou Bai and "Common Sense of First Aid for Illnesses and Injuries" co-edited by Huang Zifang and others. I was very happy at the time and immediately bought the two books back.

Now that the books were bought, naturally, I should enjoy the priority of reading them. After reading them, I felt that this kind of common medical knowledge is something that everyone should have. In the past, I had a wrong idea, thinking that first aid medical knowledge should only be possessed by people who live in the countryside and are far away from hospitals. People like me who live in the city, where there are many hospitals, don't seem to need it. Now I know that's not right, because it doesn't hurt to have any knowledge. Besides, first aid is very "urgent." Even if there is a hospital nearby, sending the patient there quickly will still be a bit slow. Furthermore, lacking this knowledge, one will be in a panic and may even make mistakes. It's better to have this common sense oneself, so that one can save oneself if possible, and if one can't save oneself, one can make proper arrangements to avoid accidents, and one won't be in a panic. I think there must be many people who have had my past wrong idea, so I wrote this passage.

Now I will talk about the content of these two books: the content of these two books is the same, but "Common Sense of First Aid for Illnesses and Injuries" is simpler and smaller, a small book that can be put in a pocket and carried around. The author of "Popular Medical First Aid" is a very famous doctor in Shanghai. The writing is very popular, and the description is very concise. It is divided into four chapters: The first chapter is on first aid treatment, from the essentials of first aid to the first aid methods for various diseases and injuries, divided into sixteen sections. The second chapter is on infectious diseases and disinfection methods, divided into three sections, explaining the types of infectious diseases, the portals of entry into the human body, the conditions of onset, prevention methods, etc., as well as various disinfection methods. The third chapter is on medicines that should be kept at home, divided into five sections, describing the dosage of medicines, preparation methods, children's dosage, and main medicines. The fourth chapter is on medical equipment that should be kept at home, divided into eleven sections, detailing all the simple and indispensable medical equipment for families.

Now it is winter, and when the weather gets cold, many people will light fires for warmth. However, one may die from carbon monoxide poisoning if one is not careful. The great geologist Mr. Ding Zaijun died of carbon monoxide poisoning. It is said that Dr. Ma Yinchu, an economist, suffered from carbon monoxide poisoning last year. Because he was aware of it, he took immediate measures to save himself and was spared an invitation from the King of Hell. Four years ago, I suffered from carbon monoxide poisoning twice in Dezhou and Peiping, vomiting a lot of blood. Fortunately, I was rescued quickly and spared my life. For ourselves and to save others, I think this kind of first aid knowledge is something that everyone should have!

My Newly Made Friends 208

— By Zhe Feng

—After reading "Wen Xin"—

Although my junior high school life has long become a spring dream of yesterday and is increasingly distant from me, recently it has allowed me to get to know several junior high school friends. Although I have never met them, their faces and personalities are exceptionally familiar.

Zhou Lehua is a very healthy young man.

Zhang Dawen is a fatherless child.

Zhu Zhiqing speaks very clearly.

Hu Fuchu is a chubby fellow.

Du Zhenyu doesn't talk much on weekdays.

They are all young people full of emotion, with a strong desire for knowledge and keen sensitivity. Since I became acquainted with them, I have been inseparable from them all day long. Sometimes we review Chinese language lectures together, sometimes we edit wall newspapers together, sometimes we visit the article hospital with a dollar, sometimes we rehearse dramas, sometimes we visit famous mountains, sometimes we hold lectures, sometimes we hold symposiums… All day long, it's either research or discussion. Our spirits seem to be fused together like milk and water.

In fact, I have also gained a lot of benefits from them: they treat me with innocent friendship and sincere hearts, which makes me deeply feel the joy of life and human sympathy. They also show me how to read books that are not written with words.

Yes, they have given me a lot, arousing my interest in research, and giving me more knowledge and methods than I gained in the past three years of junior high school. Therefore, I have indeed built a very high level of friendship with them. I have shed tears of sympathy for Lehua's dropping out of school and worried about the friendship between Dawen and Jinhua. I have also been convinced by their high-sounding arguments, and I have also been… In short, they are all friends that I will always remember in my heart.

The reason why I am able to get acquainted with these friends is thanks to our introducers, Mr. Xia Mianzun and Mr. Ye Shengtao. They not only enabled me to meet them, but also enabled them to recognize me and to recognize all of China—or it can be said, the whole world—thousands upon thousands of young people.

As Mr. Zhu Ziqing said in this book, "Mianzun and Shengtao writing the story of reading and writing in 'Wen Xin' is indeed a meritorious deed."

Therefore, we—I and the thousands upon thousands of young people who have read Wen Xin—should also agree with what Mr. Chen Wangdao said in this book: "We should thank Mr. Mianzun and Mr. Shengtao for thinking about young people, painstakingly collecting the most advanced knowledge of the present, and writing it in an easy-to-understand way, so that we young people also have the opportunity to approach it."

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

The Xi'an Incident 209

— Fang

Our country's unification had just succeeded, and the resistance against foreign aggression had just achieved victory, when suddenly an incident occurred in Xi'an. People at home and abroad were all aghast and astonished.

What is the situation in Xi'an now? What is Zhang Xueliang's purpose? And what is the attitude of the generals? The telegrams that have been sent are full of conflicting claims, and here in Xi'an, where news is blocked, we have no way to guess.

However, based on Zhang Xueliang's own character, he should not, and must not, betray the central government and commit the absurd act of kidnapping Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. Let me ask, who was it that lost the three northeastern provinces amidst the red lights and green wine? Who was it that promoted and cultivated him after he returned to the country, and brought him to his current position? Now, at a time when the resistance against the enemy is tense, he suddenly takes this extraordinary action. I ask, where is his conscience?

Moreover, now is a time when bandits and puppets are active, and the work of resisting the enemy is progressing smoothly, and there is hope of recovering lost territory. Zhang should make amends for his past mistakes and serve on the frontier, which is exactly the right time. Now he is kidnapping his leader and defending himself with troops. This kind of action is not only a betrayal of the party and the country, but is tantamount to helping the bandits and puppets to counterattack. The lack of conscience in a person has reached this point.

Tsim Sha Tsui 210

— Shi Dai

Although the season has reached late autumn, the island in the south still floats with waves of heat. There are bare-chested coolies on the pier, and men and women swimming on the beach, everything is no different from summer. This reminds me of the late autumn I spent in the north, which was constantly invaded by storms and cold—at this moment I should thank the great nature of this island, it has given me, this wanderer, infinite grace. Warm sunshine—may it forever accompany me in my life, so that the cruel winter has no chance to attack me.

It has been almost two months since I came to Hong Kong—Birmingham is suffering from malaria because he is not accustomed to the climate—we are both impoverished and cannot afford a doctor, so we can only let the disease grow—however, he has gradually improved in the past week, so I took him out to travel and play in the mountains and rivers, so that he can recover his health sooner.

Yesterday we visited "Mount Davis," and today we plan to spend the whole day visiting Kowloon. Birmingham said that he hadn't bathed in the sea for many days, so when he got to Kowloon he had to go to "Lai Chi Kok" to swim and visit "Tsim Sha Tsui."

Early in the morning, we went to the pier to take the ferry. It only costs three cents per person to get to Kowloon on the other side.

Fishing boats returning from outside the port gathered in the port like schools of fish. The faint morning light shone on the sails, and the sea was calm. After a quarter of an hour, we moved to Kowloon City.

At the end of the street market, we discovered "Tsim Sha Tsui," this long strip of countryside. "Tsim Sha Tsui" is bordered by the sea on one side, and stretches to Hung Hom on the other side. Its back is close to foreign houses and roads. It is not right to say that it is desolate here, but it cannot be regarded as a lively place either. It is best to take a walk here.

The boundless green grass is bathed in the intoxicating sunlight. Its color is more beautiful and lovely than the sea water, but it does not have the delicate tenderness of spring or the lush greenness of summer—at this time, cold dew seems to be attached to its body. Obviously, this is not the immortal dew that nourishes it, but the disaster water that destroys its life. The branches of the green trees are shaking lively, and the sea is also laughing with ripples. The air is fresh, and we feel so happy! If there wasn't dew on the grass, we would definitely roll around on it.

We walked hand in hand towards the sea. Surprisingly—that old fisherman I knew in Shek Sarp, Hong Kong, appeared here again. I happily went up to greet him…

——Uncle! Why did you come here so early this morning?

——We don't have a fixed place! We go wherever there are fish. Are you two here to play so early?

He was tidying up the fishing nets. The boat was swaying, and the fish basket was half empty. Judging from his expression, the fish probably weren't getting caught in the nets.

This old man is a small and thin man. The cheekbones on his face are unusually high, causing his cheeks to sink. His forehead is covered with several deep wrinkles of wind and dust. Although his life is very poor, his attitude seems very leisurely, and he rarely shows a sad face. He is always kind and amiable as he does his work. The sea is the source of his life, his desires, his ideals, all are entrusted to the sea, this boundless sea!

I first met him in Shek Sarp, where I went to bathe every day, so I had many opportunities to contact him. On this island in the south, besides my companion Birmingham, he—the lovely old fisherman—has become one of the people I like to approach the most. He tells me about his life experiences and his history of struggling with life, as well as many bizarre and strange stories, and even tells me his unspeakable secrets frankly, which moves me to the point of tears. He and we are both insulted and harmed, but the pain and oppression he has suffered is a deeper layer than ours, and he understands better than us how difficult life is!

The old man was busy fishing, so we didn't bother him and walked away. We couldn't bear to leave this grassland and wanted to play to our heart's content before leaving. After a while, a neat sound of footsteps came. Looking over, it was the "Indian soldiers" who came here to practice.

Those who practiced were all "Indian soldiers." They were as strong and energetic as oxen, as if they were going to the battlefield to kill the enemy. Heavy footsteps followed the orders of the officers and ran back and forth. Sometimes they practiced field warfare, sometimes they practiced cavalry changes, and sometimes they practiced live ammunition shooting! The commander—that imposing white man!—shouted various commands, dividing them into two teams, each occupying one side, and then attacking each other according to the commander's orders. The "Indian soldiers" showed no expression on their faces, simply like a machine in motion. The rifles on their shoulders were fitted with bright

Page 22

dazzling bayonets] The light threatened the sun, threatened the countryside, and threatened this colony.

My heart was oppressed by a weight, and my breathing was almost suffocated. We were silent, silent, watching their exercise, and only after they were over did we regain our normal breathing, as if we had been released from shackles. Ah! Those Indian soldiers, they are driven from colony to colony, from their own land to other places to help their enemies oppress the slaves of the colony. The bloodstains on their bodies have not yet healed, but they follow the oppressors to slaughter weak nations!

The roar of the train broke through the clear and quiet sky. The flag of the English warship fluttered. The "Indian soldiers" left in neat steps, and we also began to go to "Lai Chi Kok."

One Day in a Temporary Shelter 211

— Xin Ye

In the morning, the sky was only a little bit hazy, and I was awakened by the coughing and choking of the old man next to me. I opened my eyes and looked outside the door. Snowflakes were floating in the sky, and the howling wind shook several of the pillars in the house a little. At the top of a row of clamshell window sills, there were several sparrows chirping: as if they, like us, had come here to take refuge.

My wife was probably exhausted from being disturbed by the children last night, and was still sleeping soundly close to my body. The child was lying under her elbow, his little face was thin and yellow, looking unlike himself.

The weather last night was really cold. Lying on the straw was like lying on ice. A wave of cold air drilled into my bones, making it impossible for me to close my eyes. I just listened to the heavy sighs and low cries of sorrow. The child was clamoring for hunger and cold. My wife was reminiscing about her old home, not forgetting those thirty-odd pregnant ewes… She hoped that the war would calm down immediately, so that she could return to her warm home. But when she thought that her old home had been swallowed by artillery fire, she felt an indescribable pain in her heart!

The sky gradually brightened, and the white light slipped into the house, making everything in the hall very clear. I saw that on the dusty shrine, a spider was weaving a web in the corner, and a sense of being homeless arose from the depths of my heart—the refugees who were lying haphazardly on the straw on the ground were sitting up one by one. A stuffy and foul odor was brewing in the room, but the heavy sighs and low cries of sorrow filled the entire room again. They had not forgotten the hunger in their bellies, nor had they forgotten the homes that had been swallowed by cannons and bombs. But everyone was still worried that the cannons and bombs would one day spread to this place.

The child woke up. As soon as he opened his eyes, he clamored for something to eat, but there was nothing at this time. What could I take to give him to eat? My wife also sat up painfully, patted him, and tried all kinds of ways to coax him, but it was useless. I looked at my wife's expression and felt that something was wrong. I reached out and tried her forehead, and it was as hot as a stove. I quickly retracted my hand and said softly…

"You're sick!"

But she just shook her head, looked at me with melancholy eyes for a while, and reluctantly answered me… "No…" Her voice was so low.

Snowflakes flew down from the sky like smoke. They had not stopped from morning to noon, and were getting tighter and tighter. However, no one had been seen bringing anything to fill our hunger. Everyone was holding an empty stomach, staring blankly at the gray and dilapidated walls in a daze.

Another group of refugees threw themselves into the shelter. They were all as embarrassed as us, old, young, male, and female. Some were crying, and some were sighing.

In a not very large earth god temple, three or four hundred men and women were squeezed in, and there was no room to put a foot. Now that more and more people are crowding in, wouldn't it be necessary to break this earth god temple? But, but we are all people who have fallen into trouble, all want to escape for our lives, what discrimination is there! Food was distributed, and each person received two cold and hard dry steamed buns. Some people grabbed them and gnawed on them, and drank snow to quench their thirst. Those toothless old people could only swallow saliva while looking at these steamed buns. Although their stomachs were rumbling and clear water was constantly rising, they couldn't bite them, so what could they do!

I finished gnawing my two dry steamed buns, but my wife still hadn't eaten, but the child was holding a steamed bun and biting it mouthful by mouthful, looking like he was having a hard time eating it.

My wife was moaning softly. I was very worried, worried that she would get sick and not be able to get up. If… what would happen to the child? I really dare not think about it.

"Are you uncomfortable?" I lowered my head and kissed her forehead, which was still very hot, and couldn't help asking.

"I'm very thirsty!" She nodded spasmodically to me. But there was no place to find water here, only snow could be taken to quench her thirst. In desperation, I watched my wife's distress and finally took a handful of snow, watching my wife swallow it happily, as if she was swallowing it with relish.

More groups of refugees kept coming in, and we were squeezed even tighter.

Night gradually fell, and the room suddenly became dark and gloomy. Although the snow outside had stopped, the wind was louder than during the day. There were no lights in the room. In the darkness, sighs, cries, curses, and resentments were constantly swaying in every corner.

Dinner, as usual, was two cold and hard dry steamed buns per person.

But, where is my home, where is my hometown? From now on, where will we go to live?

Ah! The way out for women?…
